Symbol: \IncBeta

  Feature Set: dlmf-macro
	DLMF: \IncBeta{x}@{a}{b}
	DLMF-Link: dlmf.nist.gov/8.17#E1
	Maple-Alternatives: int(t^($1-1)*(1-t)^($2-1), t = 0 .. $0)
	Maple-Comment: Maple has no extra function for this macro but you can use the alternative translation, based on the DLMF definition.
	Mathematica: Beta[$0, $1, $2]
	Mathematica-Branch Cuts: (-\inf, 0)
	Mathematica-Comment: It has a branch cut for complex parameters (x in DLMF).

Symbol: \acot

  Feature Set: dlmf-macro
	Branch Cuts: (-\iunit, \iunit)
	Constraints: z not element of {0,-\iunit,+\iunit}
	DLMF: \acot@@{z}
	DLMF-Link: dlmf.nist.gov/4.23#SS2.p1
	Maple: arccot($0)
	Maple-Alternatives: I/2*ln(($0-I)/($0+I) ) || arctan(1/($0))
	Maple-Branch Cuts: (- I infinity, - I ), ( I, I infinity )
	Maple-Comment: Maple defines another branch cut than DLMF for the invert cotangent function. You can use an alternative translation to avoid that. With the arctan alternative you have the same branch cuts as DLMF. See also 'According to Arbamowitz and Stegun or arccoth needn't be uncouth' by R.M. Corless, D.J. Jeffrey, S.M. Watt.
	Maple-Constraints: 
	Maple-Link: www.maplesoft.com/support/help/maple/view.aspx?path=invtrig
	Maple-Package: 
	Mathematica: ArcCot[$0]
	Mathematica-Alternatives: 
	Mathematica-Branch Cuts: 
	Mathematica-Comment: 
	Mathematica-Constraints: 
	Mathematica-Link: reference.wolfram.com/language/ref/ArcCot.html
	Mathematica-Package: 
	Meanings: Inverse cotangent
	Number of Ats: 2
	Number of Parameters: 0
	Number of Variables: 1
	Role: dlmf-macro
